Line 1123-1130: Gets parent dentry and dir inode\n3. Line 1134-1141: Checks if inode exists\n4. Line 1143-1149: Checks for bad inode\n5. Line 1151-1152: If autom ount, returns success\n6. Line 1155-1164: Checks verifier and calls nfs_lookup_verify_inode\n7. Line 1158-1161: If nfs_lookup_verify_inode returns error, goes to out_zap_parent\n\nThe issue might be in line 1158-1161. Let me re-read the nfs_lookup_verify_inode function more carefully:\n\nFrom lines 1054-1077:\n```c\nstatic int nfs_lookup_verify_inode(struct inode *inode, unsigned int flags)\n{\n    struct nfs_server *server = NFS_SERVER(inode);\n    int ret;\n\n    if (IS_AUTOMOUNT(inode))\n        return 0;\n    /* VFS wants an on-the-wire revalidation */\n    if (flags & LOOKUP_REVAL)\n        goto out_force;\n    /* This is an open(2) */\n    if ((flags & LOOKUP_OPEN) && !(server->flags & NFS_MOUNT_NOCTO) &&\n        (S_ISREG(inode->i_mode) || S_ISDIR(inode->i_mode)))\n        goto out_force;\nout:\n    return (inode->i_nlink == 0) ? -ENOENT : 0;\nout_force:\n    if (flags & LOOKUP_RCU)\n        return -ECHILD;\n    ret = __nfs_revalidate_inode(server, inode);\n    if (ret != 0)\n        return ret;\n    goto out;\n}\n```\n\nSo when nfs_lookup_verify_inode calls __nfs_revalidate_inode and it returns an error (like -512), that error gets returned directly. Back in nfs_lookup_revalidate, when this error is returned, it triggers the error handling path that goes to out_zap_parent.\n\nAt out_zap_parent, the code invalidates the parent directory's caches and falls through to out_bad, which marks the dentry as invalid and returns 0. This is problematic because the original error code (-512) gets lost—the function returns 0 instead of propagating the actual error that occurred during inode validation.\n\nThe real issue is that nfs_lookup_verify_inode returning -512 triggers the same error handling path as parent directory invalidation scenarios, but these are fundamentally different situations. An RPC error shouldn't be treated the same way as a cache invalidation. I need to understand what -512 represents in the NFS/RPC layer to determine if it requires special handling or if the error path itself is {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01RimQyEeL1bbhQUGDikAxMX","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now I see the issue! Looking at the code path:\n\nIn `nfs_lookup_revalidate` at line 1158:\n```c\nif (nfs_lookup_verify_inode(inode, flags)) {\n    if (flags & LOOKUP_RCU)\n        return -ECHILD;\n    goto out_zap_parent;\n}\n```\n\nThe problem is that `nfs_lookup_verify_inode` can return:\n1. 0 - inode is valid\n2. Positive error (like -ENOENT) - inode needs revalidation\n3. Negative error (like -512 from RPC layer) - RPC failure\n\nThe issue is that line 1158 checks `if (nfs_lookup_verify_inode(...))` which treats ANY non-zero return as needing to go to `out_zap_parent`. But `out_zap_parent` is designed for parent directory changes, not for RPC errors!\n\nWhen `out_zap_parent` runs:\n1. It calls `nfs_zap_caches(dir)` to invalidate parent directory caches\n2. Then falls through to `out_bad`3. At `out_bad`, it returns 0 (success), which tells VFS the dentry is invalid\n\nBut this is wrong when the error is an RPC failure! The dentry shouldn't be marked as invalid just because an RPC call failed with -512. The problem is that the code treats all non-zero returns from `nfs_lookup_verify_inode` the same way, when it should distinguish between:1. Valid errors that mean revalidation is needed (like -ENOENT, other transient errors)\n2. Fatal errors that indicate a real problem with the inode and shouldn't result in just marking the dentry invalid\n\nLet me look at what errors `__nfs_revalidate_inode` returns and how they should be handled. Looking back at the __nfs_revalidate_inode function (lines 930-996), the error path at line 961-970 shows:\n\n\nWhen `__nfs_revalidate_inode` encounters an error, it handles -ESTALE specially by clearing caches and marking non-directory inodes as stale. Other errors are logged but the inode state isn't modified in the same way, suggesting they're treated as transient failures rather than definitive proof the inode is invalid.\n\nThe issue appears to be that `nfs_lookup_revalidate` doesn't distinguish between different error types when `nfs_lookup_verify_inode` fails. An -ESTALE error (indicating the inode is genuinely stale) warrants invalidating the dentry and parent, but an RPC error like -512 should probably be propagated to the caller rather than silently invalidating the dentry. The current code treats all non-zero returns the same way by jumping to `out_zap_parent`, which may be too aggressive for transient network failures.","signature":"EpIVCkYICxgCKkBJsWRAookbumbyfrJjhVgh6YC7s2dzHULWx4KDKF8EQSn8Ob9X2NHP+V+/jsivU1Mmk4sK7hx1Oh8QCa7TD4ssEgyHFEGbqqZqIJL09RYaDHIOoI0ERn6JIqGkSyIwWJfOIVqBwdyxJlq6f0MKi6gU2AV6hgn3qKbznh08brvTiy+PDUfqliwXCgYauU2CKvkTexX1RFQJUuTw251dBTdoqlQImM9ZY8VvB3La8GW/Ok7EgRiHtiyauynYgcDoiXyYgm7ts5UHJDGrKvxWGO/HSPrbBsyxbV08lcKEMwVDmjcS5QOEf5N9NMm0uugTsQQ7IhRjJqZsXqQF6DMQpddAFNjGYuVNqToqpEU4CVnLmdGhVOWfJlThqcfiIC0ksSdyIMyk51+BfRvwMeSb6hNJxFOHX2oMwuQAOfU8q1SoMySKaV1/G7YnldEXSOk7GbyqptljFx0ZLzGlgLMx48rMgPL46/+BWHa5S7iHKoypEqxsCCqhWIRiw23nZp2GXvXj8QuooWRUuNZVdma3kKVHQLdj1ihvdnB6NdocuaAr82LOUshwdxqiSK/cSnlRbiT+HJMmldzQX5PiYICJFgk2buzJu6B3tjj5IkgM38pJdonEToVosndKB4dmn+VfbchQ7KpfIIuLIms+v5LJ+M+wA7lPiEwq1iNsR3XtO9VEV+pAX9Q8LmnoJfZE9p+s3uN2MdVewnGwXOSOD4qYjRASC4Dh9+MI5ia4HQFlyd1HWTUgJTf68nfz04SYgOUpj3V8Mb2Irwkd85aPelfGwIaV7beTqoWk4cFMjyHFeZNrCUkCOZahfN2bDN04GhXNs+Pas+Iy3RBxoZzkux59f5JxE6kzVse4E262nsHpFU8H0Ke2dFSnaOtj7v2n2UPOdOnkJn0MS/NrGPn9x6aEIyIan3izYbDE/wvVJeOcYhIcnrfJkX+YCYGUOQbF2VvSrubhgdHKmWMspMGzJHXldZt3cou9+Fmvpqv3O6JidPErhOB+GLiccyIDEIUjnQHRwY3Hj63CsMitB7cXGiKy9B3t2enS7N/ZAiTWxydTAmNOoaIEavH3EFrVKFKPD/KA0raN8P8/vorR+tjFjySMgAprPdWHuDTiDR0w7IqUM7gVz2St1jU2aTYMeHWsT5kUngTz0nxn36ksocemDPN0SjhnC9Or2KZZlF+e+BRVXFzaz4IhG4nktu1v3upykQO4SvqeYFRRSMHnvY+R+OwAwRfH4y1Rkb299W4LQXXUWkBDKXxrvk2fN7QTekmTdLlMLsBUEFNC+6qpsJcRjtmkjNvnMuxlM32z8FyGSdTJGIulA65QEtuypPrywwRu/aiR1F4xOKFXApEI2C8hGR0KOG1HY1I2ziPar4hAQHZYSuCdT5m/WtPt4uivrg1tTzFjlpnsOODJMscnfCQOtdB/aTtpTDcA9p/OiiB06paZ+HOGnx81SKPLsQENFDlKehWGIW9wIXu9oK/A8i7q+aULKbpOYPFjgBSoKL4Kl4XtH9j7aBNUy9Ur4FaeONEV4T0OQOYODEf4EjbGGrex2iZf1mHNHsGvsDLfYHSpk6GbhLnca7KAhljreRXoMAlK4QT1KcUo8bbmB1B9qB+KJqXWHQp5h6lI0JEZLUCbbn909IpXYpTvklQZog3RsvJv0FLIdh76gpkWwBkyi66xWkulQDpSZiyyWOQO2ob7opOc/4G5Dmr2vY671uGpWqzslrFA55ZejDVjZZZ7Yt0vity/QnedpgAs4vDzB9KN1rP48SNrZ3r8AuU2M6RqnWFaHKIcHbywDyUZBpIYVPpuj9i2mfd0MNbTUf0Vm/j6Nj7N7as143MUdQB9o3gGK/4bVX+bAMQOHKxPnT9N5nWz5H0p1qLnDuyxAN7F32QbR5S3X2p/2f9LNjQilaytuCdriHsmZq9xoDZhJmoPT+/5+/4+W5lRwA5lIRYakSQkOx0fA2oU {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01F9eRo8a7cGBELJW7xLvRyu","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now I see the issue! The bug is at line 1158-1161:\n\n```c\nif (nfs_lookup_verify_inode(inode, flags)) {\n    if (flags & LOOKUP_RCU)        return -ECHILD;    goto out_zap_parent;\n}\n```\n\nThe problem is:1. `nfs_lookup_verify_inode` can return various error codes (negative values) when __nfs_revalidate_inode fails\n2. When it returns a negative error code (like -512), the `if` check treats it as TRUE (non-zero)\n3. So it goes to `out_zap_parent` which clears parent directory caches\n4. Then it falls through to `out_bad` which marks the dentry as invalid (returns 0)\n5. This causes the VFS to remove the dentry from the cache\n6. When autofs has a mount on this dentry, removing the dentry causes the mount to be unmounted!The issue is that RPC errors (like -512 which seems to be a transient or timeout error) should NOT cause the dentry to be marked as invalid. When nfs_lookup_verify_inode returns an error (e.g., -512 from RPC call failure), the code treats any non-zero return value identically - it goes to out_zap_parent which clears parent directory caches and then falls through to out_bad, ultimately returning 0 (marking the dentry as invalid). This causes VFS to drop the dentry from cache. However, RPC errors (like -512 from network issues) should not automatically invalidate the dentry. Instead, they should be propagated to the caller or handled as transient failures. The issue is that the code does not distinguish between errors that indicate parent directory changes (which require cache invalidation) and RPC errors from the getattr() call (which are transient network failures). When autofs mount points depend on this dentry, marking it invalid causes the entire mount tree to be unmounted, even though the RPC failure is transient. When nfs_lookup_verify_inode returns an error (e.g., -512 from RPC call failure), the code treats any non-zero return value identically - it goes to out_zap_parent which clears parent directory caches and then falls through to out_bad, ultimately returning 0 (marking the dentry as invalid). The issue is that the code does not distinguish between errors that indicate parent directory changes (which require cache invalidation) and RPC errors from the getattr() call (which are transient network failures).
